### Round 4 | macro | run_macro

- agent_name: macro

- status: success

- task_received: Current reasoning phase: portfolio_screening. Agent framing mode: portfolio_neutral. Do not treat neutral aromatic as settled. Execute exactly one registry-backed macro capability: `screen_rotor_torsion_topology`. Screen the remaining highest-priority coverage-debt hypothesis TICT directly and deliver a bounded summary of rotor density, torsion candidate count, branching/peripheral rotor topology, and whether the observed topology is strong, moderate, or weak structural support for a TICT-style mechanism relative to a neutral aromatic interpretation. Do not perform multi-step follow-up, external comparison, or global mechanism adjudication.

- task_completion_status: completed

- task_completion: Task completed successfully within current macro capability.

- task_understanding: The task is to perform a direct structural screen of the TICT hypothesis by analyzing the rotor and torsion topology of the molecule. This involves summarizing rotor density, counting torsion candidates, assessing branching and peripheral rotor topology, and evaluating the strength of this topology as structural support for a TICT mechanism relative to a neutral aromatic interpretation. The analysis must be bounded, single-step, and use only registry-backed macro capabilities without global adjudication or multi-step follow-up.

- reasoning_summary: The portfolio screening has directly weakened the ICT hypothesis via donor-acceptor layout screening, leaving TICT as the highest-priority unresolved alternative. The molecule has a rotor-rich topology with 14 rotatable bonds and torsion candidates, significant branching points, and a complex aromatic ring system. A direct rotor/torsion topology screen will provide bounded structural evidence to assess whether the observed rotor density and torsion topology strongly, moderately, or weakly support a TICT mechanism compared to the neutral aromatic hypothesis.
Capability limit note: Only deterministic low-cost single-molecule macro analysis is available. The screening will use the shared prepared structure context for accurate topology analysis. No multi-step or global mechanism adjudication is possible.

- execution_plan: Use deterministic_macro_structure_scan to execute the bounded registry-backed macro capability `screen_rotor_torsion_topology` with focus areas: TICT hypothesis, rotor density, torsion candidates, branching topology, structural support strength. ### Round 5 | macro | run_macro

- agent_name: macro

- status: success

- task_received: Current reasoning phase: portfolio_screening. Agent framing mode: portfolio_neutral. Do not treat neutral aromatic as settled. Execute exactly one registry-backed macro capability: `screen_intramolecular_hbond_preorganization`. Screening focus hypothesis: ESIPT. Using the shared prepared structure, provide a bounded direct screen for any intramolecular H-bond candidate summary, typed donor/acceptor preorganization summary, and local preorganization geometry status relevant to proton transfer. The goal is to determine whether ESIPT can be directly screened out or remains structurally credible enough to stay in the portfolio. Do not decide the global mechanism.

- task_completion_status: completed

- task_completion: Task completed successfully within current macro capability.

- task_understanding: The task is to perform a bounded direct structural screen for intramolecular hydrogen bond (H-bond) preorganization relevant to excited-state intramolecular proton transfer (ESIPT). This involves analyzing the shared prepared molecular geometry to identify any intramolecular H-bond candidates, characterize typed donor and acceptor preorganization, and assess local geometric features that could facilitate proton transfer. The goal is to determine whether ESIPT remains structurally credible or can be directly screened out, without making any global mechanism decisions.

- reasoning_summary: Given that the portfolio screening has already directly screened ICT and TICT hypotheses, the remaining coverage debt is for ESIPT. The current reasoning phase is pairwise contraction anchored on the neutral aromatic hypothesis versus TICT, with ESIPT still untested. The shared prepared structure context is available and should be leveraged to perform a low-cost, deterministic macro-level analysis of intramolecular H-bond preorganization. This will provide bounded structural evidence to either support or weaken ESIPT's credibility in the portfolio.
Capability limit note: The macro capability is limited to deterministic, low-cost single-molecule structural and geometry proxy analysis using the shared prepared structure. It cannot perform excited-state relaxation modeling, packing simulations, or global mechanism adjudication.

- execution_plan: Use deterministic_macro_structure_scan to execute the bounded registry-backed macro capability `screen_intramolecular_hbond_preorganization` with focus areas: intramolecular H-bond candidates, donor/acceptor preorganization, local geometry for proton transfer. Planned local steps: [shared_context_load] Load the shared prepared structure context and reuse its descriptors. [focus_selection] Translate the Planner instruction into one bounded registry-backed macro capability. [topology_analysis] Collect deterministic structural evidence for `screen_intramolecular_hbond_preorganization` from the available structure source. [geometry_proxy_analysis] Summarize only bounded local structural or geometry-proxy outputs and record any missing deliverables.

- result_summary: Bounded intramolecular H-bond preorganization screening inspected reusable prepared geometry for generic H-bond candidates and typed donor/acceptor contact cues without making any mechanism judgment. The macro scan recorded aromatic_atom_count=72, hetero_atom_count=2, branch_point_count=34, rotatable_bond_count=14, planarity_proxy=0.987043, compactness_proxy=0.964276, and conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0.
Key proxies: aromatic_atom_count=72, hetero_atom_count=2, branch_point_count=34, conjugation_proxy=18.987, flexibility_proxy=32.0, rotatable_bond_count=14, aromatic_ring_count=12, ring_system_count=12, donor_acceptor_partition_proxy=0.0, planarity_proxy=0.987043, compactness_proxy=0.964276, conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0.

- remaining_local_uncertainty: Macro evidence alone cannot resolve excited-state relaxation behavior or external consistency; unresolved local gap: Macro evidence is limited to single-molecule low-cost structural and geometry proxies, so it still cannot resolve excited-state relaxation behavior, aggregation-state packing, or external consistency.

The goal is to summarize and interpret planarity_proxy, compactness_proxy, principal_span_proxy, and conformer_dispersion_proxy observables from the available shared prepared structure context. The interpretation should focus on whether these geometry proxies support an aromatic-core-dominant neutral aromatic organization or a TICT-favoring geometry characterized by pronounced twisting and flexible donor-acceptor separation. No global mechanism decision or external evidence is to be made or requested. The summary should explicitly note any limitations due to single-conformer analysis.

- reasoning_summary: Given the current shared prepared structure context with 10 conformers and a selected conformer, the macro capability 'screen_planarity_compactness' can deterministically analyze geometry proxies such as planarity, compactness, principal span, and conformer dispersion. These proxies are critical to discriminate between the neutral aromatic hypothesis, which would show high planarity and compactness consistent with an aromatic core, versus the TICT hypothesis, which would manifest as lower planarity and higher conformer dispersion due to twisting and donor-acceptor separation. The existing data shows a very large aromatic scaffold with high planarity and compactness proxies, and a conformer dispersion proxy of 1.0, indicating limited conformer variability. This analysis will provide bounded internal evidence to support closure justification for the pairwise comparison.
Capability limit note: The macro capability is limited to deterministic low-cost single-molecule geometry-proxy analysis using the shared prepared structure context. It cannot resolve excited-state relaxation behavior, aggregation-state packing, or external consistency. The analysis is limited by the single-conformer selection and does not include global mechanism adjudication or external evidence integration.

- final_hypothesis_rationale: The molecule is an extremely large, heavily arylated, donor-acceptor-poor boron-containing hydrocarbon with dominant aromatic-core character, very low hetero-atom burden, no ESIPT-ready motif, and no meaningful donor-acceptor partitioning. TICT was the only credible challenger because of rotor richness, but both internal topology evidence and external close-family precedent indicate that rotor richness here is distributed over a large aromatic scaffold rather than organized into a focused donor-acceptor twisting architecture. The newly completed planarity/compactness geometry-proxy screen closes the main internal gap and further supports a neutral-aromatic, rigid-core-dominated interpretation.

- capability_assessment: Macro was the correct capability for the missing closure task because the required observable was exactly a registry-backed geometry-proxy screen. Verifier supplementation is already sufficient and no additional verifier call is necessary. Microscopic was not the correct route for the prior failed attempt because the requested capability was macro-native rather than an Amesp action.

- stagnation_assessment: No scientific stagnation is present. The prior issue was procedural misrouting, not evidentiary exhaustion. This round resolved that blockage by successfully executing the intended macro task, so the case has advanced materially.

- contraction_reason: Pairwise contraction remains appropriate because coverage_debt_hypotheses is empty, all screened alternatives remain weakened, verifier supplementation for neutral aromatic vs TICT is sufficient, and the missing internal pairwise closure task has now been completed.
